;==========================================================================================================

; Technical information about modding this file:
; - the initial capital a faction is always of first settlement listed in this file (irrespectively of the presence of the hidden resource capital)
; - the engine takes names for rebel "sub_faction" from the names for that faction defined in the (descr_names.txt). So: if in this file, you place a name from the another faction's list, there'll be a nameless general/princess etc.
; - a general (named character) can lead any unit => don't bother adding Bodyguards for him, it doesn't matter (even better: you may assign a strange unit for the initial generals).
; - most common source of crash is when you combine here a building-line for cities with a specific building for castles (or vice-versa).

; Bear in mind that:
; - there're no "hero_ability" in the SSHIP (yet? you can do it!)
; - only 24 buildings are visible in-game in the city panel (the rest can be seen through the building panel, but it's ackward)
; - the AI doesn't transform castles into cities (or vice versa) so what's defined here, will stay in the game

;==========================================================================================================

; Starting positions of the factions:
; - the number of troops is usually adjusted to the income of the faction with the goal to leave 10-20% budget surplus.
; - the merchants should be placed on the right resources to make the initial income (even though the AI has the habit of moving it away).
; - diplomats can be placed next to the factions we'd like the AI to make initial deals with.
; - the other agents should stay around capitals to make the player making his initial choices (the AI can see all settlements so there's no need to show it anything with the agents).
; - each faction should have princess(es) as a children of the FL/FM so that they will CoA at some point - so that there's a supply of princesses.
; - for the convenience of the player, the order of the buildings in settlements should be: core building - wonder - roads - farms - ports - military - other (or maybe not...)

;==========================================================================================================

; Slave faction settlements and starting armies
; - initial large slave armies are a problem for the AI factions (it's bad at assessing how much own units does it need)
; -  then the player can exploit the situation (wait until a the garrison bleeds out, and only then attacke )
; conclusion: do not make large garrisons, just a few units will do!

;==========================================================================================================

;==========================================================================================================
;----------- RESOURCES ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

; Placement of resources - take into account:
; (1) historicity:
; --- some provinces were famous for exporting certain resources (eg. salt near Krakow, wool in England, wine along Rhein, in Hungary, or in Monemvasia).
; --- the overall balance in the income from provinces and their development over centuries (eg. often provinces rich in gold stayed poor nonetheless).
; (2) how the trade between provinces is generated by the M2TW engine:
; --- a province trades with the neighbouring provinces: the more land borders (even over the impassable terrain), the more trade connections.
; --- only sea trade for the islands (need to have plenty of resources to be at par with other provinces - but the risk is they'll become the destination of exports from large cities).
; --- no trade of the same good: the neighbouring provinces do not trade the same resource.
; --- the resources signify only EXPORTED resources, the aboundance of those utilised/consumed in the province doesn't matter.
; (3) merchants' profitability:
; --- a resource close to the capital will not be profitable anywhere on the map - so if you have textiles or glass close to capital, your merchants won't trade it in the game 
; --- stacking of resources make a place more profitable and it should be put in the places famous for resources - where it would be historical to see a merchant at work
; (4) visual aspects:
; --- don't place a resource just in front of a settlement because it's name tag would cover it
; --- many resources will be close to settlements, but try to spread them also to far away corners
; --- the pics shown on the map (they play differently with different textures - sometimes they're partially "drowned" into the ground)
; (5) prices of resources
; --- some resources are more profitable - think of it in balancing the income of a province.
; --- mines would provide additional income - so some provinces may get much richer after they're built-up.
; (6) gameplay considerations
; --- they should be spread across the map to make it (map) relevant in more places; in other words: many areas of the map are never visited so the resources may give a reason to.
; --- trade should probably play larger role in overall income so one may place more resources and increase their prices.

; AVAILABLE RESOURCES:
;	iron -> Metals		ivory -> Oil		tobacco -> Salt		chocolate -> Glass		sulfur -> Linen
;	coal -> Herbs		dogs -> Fruits		camels -> Honey		tin -> Luxury Goods		elephants -> Cattle
;	gold, silver, marble, timber, slaves, amber, textiles, dyes, silk, cotton, furs, wool, spices, sugar, wine, grain, fish

; temporary remark for moding: if the NAME OF THE PROVINCE is written in the CAPITAL letters, it means that the set of resources and their placement were thougth out for SSHIP 097

; remember that there's a hardcoded limit for the number of times you may use one resource: 186.

; as a rule, in the SSHIP the resources should not be positioned on a road

;=========================================================================================================== SCANDINAVIA
;
; furs and timber are present in many Scandinavia provinces are given due to both historical considerations and also to the M2TW engine mechanics: provinces do not trade with the same resources
; (thus placing these resources in each province DISables unhistorical trade between them, but enables the very historical overseas exports with the warehouses - this is even more historical since they'll be build rightly late, perhaps late 13c.)

;=========================================================================================================== SLAVE
;--- Slave -----
; the settlements have usually high level of the "builder" chain because the AI doesn't know it is a pre-requisit of many buildings so it would be hampered in building up the settlements
; however, they rarely have higher levels of Landowners buildings - because the slave faction would recruit then many Knights units and make the AI facitions life too difficult
; exception: if there's an automatic siege, then there's Landowners (no problem for the AI, and after the siege it'll have access to knights)

ai_label		slave_faction

;======================================================================================================= INDEPENDENT ARMIES
;----------- INDEPENDENT ARMIES
; keep them small (ca. 7 units) because they provide more headache for the AI factions than for the player
; each army should be lead by a named character, not a general
; the garrisons in the settlements - the bodyguard should be heavy infantry and no cavalry units
; armies in the field : bodyguard should the standard knights, perhaps mainly cavalry
; to be watched: the slave faction actively recruits new units that may end up in
